Neptune is the outermost planet of the Solar System, orbiting approximately 4.5 billion kilometers (2.8 astronomical units) from the Sun. Its discovery in 1846 by Urbain Le Verrier, based on mathematical predictions, marked a significant milestone in astronomy. Neptune is notable for its atmosphere, which is heated and enriched by methane, a gas that forms a high-altitude methane cloud deck. The planet's rings, discovered in 1989 by Voyager 2, are believed to be composed of debris from the early Solar System. Neptune's proximity to the Sun makes its year shorter than that of Uranus, though it has a slightly longer orbital period than Uranus.

In 2004 and 2005, five new satellites of Neptune were discovered: Despina, Galatea, Larissa, Proteus, and Naiad. Voyager 2's encounter with Neptune in 1989 was pivotal, as it provided critical data for understanding the outer Solar System. The discovery of Pluto as a dwarf planet in 2006, and the identification of additional satellites in the 2010s, further enriched our knowledge of the Solar System.

The Kuiper Belt, a vast disc of small bodies located beyond Neptune's orbit, extends from the orbit of Neptune (30 AU) to approximately 50 AU from the Sun. It is home to several dwarf planets, including Pluto, along with numerous small moons. The Kuiper Belt represents a significant portion of the Solar System's outer regions, accounting for 20 times the width and 20 to 200 times the mass of the asteroid belt.

The ongoing exploration of the Kuiper Belt continues to reveal new insights into the formation and dynamics of the outer Solar System.

The term "mach" is a dimensionless quantity used in aerodynamics to denote the ratio of an object's speed to the speed of sound in the same medium. It is named after Austrian physicist and philosopher Ernst Mach. The mach number is calculated as the ratio of the object's speed to the local speed of sound. For example, an object moving at the speed of sound has a mach number of 1, while supersonic objects have a mach number greater than 1. The concept is widely used in fields such as aerospace engineering, aviation, and ballistics to describe the speed of vehicles relative to the speed of sound.

The umayyad period in Islamic history is marked by significant developments in governance, postal services, and administration. The umayyads, led by figures such as Abd al-Malik and Marwan II, established a regular postal service, which later evolved into the modern postal system. This postal service facilitated the movement of correspondence, troops, and goods across the Islamic world. The umayyad caliph, Abd al-Malik, introduced postal carriages that could carry up to 100 men, enhancing military operations. The postal system was further refined by his successors, including Umar bin Abbad, who built caravanserais along trade routes. The umayyad Empire's postal network played a crucial role in governance, benefiting both government officials and private correspondents.

The umayyad Empire faced criticism for promoting a form of autocratic rule (mulk) rather than a true caliphate, as perceived by later Islamic historians. This was partly due to their reliance on religious scholars for governance, which they considered a divine appointment rather than a partnership with scholars. The umayyads also faced challenges in expanding their postal network, with Caliph al-Mu'ayyad funding the postal service in 800 AD. The postal system was integral to the administration of the empire, supporting both military and civil operations.

The Bharat Ratna is the highest civilian award of India, established in 1954. It is awarded to individuals who have made exceptional contributions to any field of human endeavor. The award is conferred without discrimination based on race, occupation, position, or gender. The recommendations for the Bharat Ratna are made by the Prime Minister of India, with a maximum of three nominees awarded per year. The recipients receive a sanad (a certificate signed by the President) and a peepal-shaped medallion. Notably, the award has been expanded to include any field of human endeavor since 2011. The Bharat Ratna is the seventh highest civilian award in India and is preceded by the Padma Vibhushan, Padma Bhushan, and the Shanti Swarup. The award is conferred in recognition of exceptional service or performance of the highest order. 

The Bharat Ratna has been awarded to several distinguished individuals, including S. Radhakrishnan, Atal Bihari Vajpayee, and Nelson Mandela. The award is a symbol of India's highest civilian honor, and recipients are ranked seventh in the Indian order of precedence. The Bharat Ratna is a testament to the extraordinary contributions of individuals who have dedicated their lives to serving the nation. 

Answer: Bharat Ratna
